# Task: Map Test Coverage Gaps in Kafka Consumer Group Coordinator

**Repository:** apache/kafka
**Output:** Write your analysis to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md`

## Objective

Identify test coverage gaps in Kafka's consumer group coordinator. The group coordinator manages consumer group membership, partition assignment, and offset commits for Kafka consumers.

## Scope

Focus on:
- `core/src/main/scala/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinator.scala` — main coordinator logic
- `core/src/test/scala/unit/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinatorTest.scala` — existing tests
- `core/src/main/scala/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupMetadata.scala` — group state machine

## Content Expectations

Your analysis must:
1. **Identify at least 5 specific failure modes** that are not tested in `GroupCoordinatorTest.scala`
2. **Propose a regression test** for each failure mode (class name, test method signature, key assertions)
3. **Estimate the coverage delta** each proposed test would add (which code paths would it hit)
4. **Label risk level**: HIGH / MEDIUM / LOW

## Output Format

Write to `/workspace/coverage_analysis.md`:

```markdown
# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Kafka Consumer Group Coordinator

## Summary

## Failure Modes and Proposed Tests

### Failure Mode 1: [Name]
- **Risk**: HIGH/MEDIUM/LOW
- **Code Location**: GroupCoordinator.scala ~line NNN
- **Description**: [What failure scenario is untested]
- **Proposed Test**:
  ```java
  @Test
  public void testXxx() { ... }
  ```
- **Coverage Delta**: [Which code paths this test would exercise]

[Repeat for 5+ failure modes]

## File References
```

- Each gap must reference a specific file and approximate location
- Do NOT run the tests yourself — write the test file and the evaluation system validates independently

# Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Kafka Consumer Group Coordinator

## Summary

The Kafka consumer group coordinator (`GroupMetadataManager.java`, 8,822 lines) has extensive test coverage with 386 test methods in `GroupMetadataManagerTest.java`. However, critical failure modes and edge cases remain untested, particularly in:

- **Error recovery paths** during member deserialization and metadata updates
- **Concurrent operation scenarios** (member join/leave/metadata update races)
- **Complex state transitions** during group deletion and member fencing
- **Asynchronous regex resolution** with concurrent member departure
- **Offset management** edge cases and deletion scenarios

This analysis identifies **8 high-risk untested failure modes** that could lead to data inconsistency, silent failures, or incorrect group state management.

---

## Failure Modes and Proposed Tests

### Failure Mode 1: Malformed Embedded Consumer Protocol Deserialization
- **Risk**: MEDIUM
- **Code Location**: `GroupMetadataManager.java` ~line 1873
- **Description**: When deserializing embedded consumer protocol metadata during member updates, if the metadata is malformed (truncated, corrupted, or versioned incorrectly), the current code at line 1873 logs a warning: "Malformed embedded consumer protocol in subscription deserialization". However, there is no explicit test verifying that:
  1. The error doesn't cause silent state corruption
  2. The group state remains valid after the error
  3. Subsequent member operations (rebalance, heartbeat) work correctly
  4. Error is properly propagated to client response

The current test suite has no dedicated test for this recovery path, relying only on implicit coverage through successful deserialization paths.

Deletion during PREPARING_REBALANCE state (should prevent deletion)\n  4. Cascading effect: group tombstone \u2192 member tombstones \u2192 offset tombstones (ordering)\n  5. Re-creation of same group immediately after deletion (state leakage)\n  6. Metrics state after deletion (should cleanup counters)\n\nIncomplete deletion can leave orphaned metadata, cause memory leaks, or allow stale data to be served in future group creations.\n\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```java\n  @Test\n  public void testGroupDeletionWithPendingOffsetCommit() throws Exception {\n      String groupId = \"test-group\";\n      String memberId = \"member-1\";\n\n      // Setup: Create group with member and committed offsets\n      addConsumerGroupMember(groupId, memberId, \"instance-1\",\n          Arrays.asList(\"topic-1\"), null);\n\n      ConsumerGroup group = groupMetadataManager.consumerGroup(groupId);\n      assertEquals(ConsumerGroupState.STABLE, group.state());\n\n      // Commit offset for topic-1 partition 0\n      OffsetAndMetadata offset = new OffsetAndMetadata(100, \"\",\n          time.milliseconds());\n      group.offsetManager().put(\n          new TopicPartition(\"topic-1\", 0),\n          offset\n      );\n      assertTrue(group.offsetManager().contains(new TopicPartition(\"topic-1\", 0)));\n\n      // Trigger group deletion (e.g., explicit DeleteGroups API)\n      deleteGroup(groupId);\n\n      // Verify group still exists briefly (tombstones written asynchronously)\n      ConsumerGroup deletingGroup = groupMetadataManager.consumerGroup(groupId);\n      assertNotNull(deletingGroup);\n\n      // Wait for deletion to complete\n      time.sleep(1000); // Allow async operations\n      groupMetadataManager.onUnloaded(); // Flush tombstones\n\n      // Verify complete cleanup:\n      // 1. Group is removed\n      ConsumerGroup deletedGroup = groupMetadataManager.consumerGroup(groupId);\n      assertNull(deletedGroup);\n\n      // 2. Offsets are removed\n      // 3. Member records are tombstoned\n      // 4. Recreating group has fresh state\n      addConsumerGroupMember(groupId, \"member-2\", \"instance-2\",\n          Arrays.asList(\"topic-1\"), null);\n      ConsumerGroup recreatedGroup = groupMetadataManager.consumerGroup(groupId);\n\n      assertNotNull(recreatedGroup);\n      assertEquals(1, recreatedGroup.numMembers());\n      assertEquals(0, recreatedGroup.offsetManager().size()); // No orphaned offsets!\n  }\n  ```\n\n- **Coverage Delta**:\n  - Full execution of `maybeDeleteGroup()` deletion conditions (lines 8548-8597)\n  - Tests cascading tombstone generation for members and offsets (lines 8607-8648)\n  - Exercises offset manager cleanup path (interaction with OffsetMetadataManager)\n  - Hits member record removal with tombstone writes\n  - Validates group state machine during deletion (state transitions)\n  - Tests metrics cleanup (member count decrement)\n\n---\n\n### Failure Mode 5: Schema Exception During Member Metadata Replay\n- **Risk**: MEDIUM\n- **Code Location**: `GroupMetadataManager.java` ~lines 1291, 1372, 1379 (member metadata deserialization in `classicGroupJoin()`, replay methods)\n- **Description**: When the coordinator replays persisted member metadata from __consumer_offsets, various serialization exceptions can occur:\n  1. **SchemaException** (line 1291, 1372, 1379) - Version mismatch or corrupted schema\n  2. **UnsupportedVersionException** (line 1379) - Newer version not supported\n  3. **InvalidRecordException** - Truncated or checksum failure\n\nCurrent test coverage only implicitly handles success paths. There are **no explicit tests** for recovery when:\n- Coordinator loads group with corrupted member record\n- Partial replay fails mid-batch\n- Schema version upgrade causes deserialization errors\n- Member state is inconsistent after exception\n\nThis can cause:\n- Silent loss of member information\n- Group state corruption\n- Duplicate member IDs on recovery\n\n- **Proposed Test**:\n  ```java\n  @Test\n  public void testClassicGroupReplayWithSchemaException() throws Exception {\n      String groupId = \"test-group\";\n      String memberId = \"member-1\";\n\n      // Setup: Simulate coordinator loading group from log with corrupted member record\n      ClassicGroup group = new ClassicGroup(\n          groupId,\n          GroupState.Stable,\n          time,\n          metrics\n      );\n\n      // Create member metadata record with invalid schema bytes\n      byte[] corruptedMemberBytes = new byte[] {\n          0x00, 0x01, 0x02 // Truncated/invalid member schema\n      };\n\n      ClassicGroupMemberMetadataKey memberKey = new ClassicGroupMemberMetadataKey()\n          .setGroupId(groupId)\n          .setMemberId(memberId);\n\n      ClassicGroupMemberMetadataValue memberValue =\n          ClassicGroupMemberMetadataValue.read(\n              new ByteBuffer(corruptedMemberBytes) // Will throw SchemaException\n          );\n\n      // Attempt to replay corrupted member record\n      try {\n          groupMetadataManager.replay(memberKey, memberValue);\n          fail(\"Should have thrown SchemaException\");\n      } catch (SchemaException e) {\n          // Expected\n      }\n\n      // Verify group recovery path:\n      // 1. # Test Coverage Gap Analysis: Kafka Consumer Group Coordinator

## Summary

The Kafka consumer group coordinator (`GroupMetadataManager.java`, 8,822 lines) has extensive test coverage with 386 test methods in `GroupMetadataManagerTest.java`. However, critical failure modes and edge cases remain untested, particularly in:

- **Error recovery paths** during member deserialization and metadata updates
- **Concurrent operation scenarios** (member join/leave/metadata update races)
- **Complex state transitions** during group deletion and member fencing
- **Asynchronous regex resolution** with concurrent member departure
- **Offset management** edge cases and deletion scenarios

This analysis identifies **8 high-risk untested failure modes** that could lead to data inconsistency, silent failures, or incorrect group state management.

---

## Failure Modes and Proposed Tests

### Failure Mode 1: Malformed Embedded Consumer Protocol Deserialization
- **Risk**: MEDIUM
- **Code Location**: `GroupMetadataManager.java` ~line 1873
- **Description**: When deserializing embedded consumer protocol metadata during member updates, if the metadata is malformed (truncated, corrupted, or versioned incorrectly), the current code at line 1873 logs a warning: "Malformed embedded consumer protocol in subscription deserialization". However, there is no explicit test verifying that:
  1. The error doesn't cause silent state corruption
  2. The group state remains valid after the error
  3. Subsequent member operations (rebalance, heartbeat) work correctly
  4. Error is properly propagated to client response

The current test suite has no dedicated test for this recovery path, relying only on implicit coverage through successful deserialization paths.

- **Proposed Test**:
  ```java
  @Test
  publ
